<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1418790f-4bbf-4d72-b9fc-fe9495a8d5ef'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="review_2215331354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215331354" />
    <a title="Fran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74816651-fran"><img alt="Fran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586773357p2/74816651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2215331354?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fran" href="/user/show/74816651-fran">Fran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74816651-fran?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74816651-fran?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2215331354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4839916267767914007">On New Year's Eve, Maledictus Maggot, legal officer of His Excellency the Minister of Pitch Darkness, arrives in the laboratory of Shadow Sorcery Minister Beelzebub Preposteror, to remind Beelzebub that he's behind on his contract to wreak havoc on the world, and that if he does not make good before midnight he'll be <i>foreclose</i>...<br/><br/>I didn't get to read this one as a child, I was well into my adult days when I got my hands on it. Why do I mention this? Because the child in me is still angry she didn</span>
  <span id="freeText4839916267767914007" style="display:none">On New Year's Eve, Maledictus Maggot, legal officer of His Excellency the Minister of Pitch Darkness, arrives in the laboratory of Shadow Sorcery Minister Beelzebub Preposteror, to remind Beelzebub that he's behind on his contract to wreak havoc on the world, and that if he does not make good before midnight he'll be <i>foreclose</i>...<br /><br />I didn't get to read this one as a child, I was well into my adult days when I got my hands on it. Why do I mention this? Because the child in me is still angry she didn't get to read this and enjoy it how only children can. <br /><br />In this book, Ende brews a potent dose of comic fantasy. The story bubbles thanks to the mischievous wordplay, splashing fun with comical incidents, and has been spiked with just the right dose of verse to make children laugh without annoying the parents who may be reading to them. It's true that at times the prose, perhaps because of the translation from the German, is not always graceful, but the sheer momentum of the plot and the raw power of Ende's inventiveness suffice to carry readers all the way through this extravaganza.<br /><br />The two main characters are animals, a cat -Mauricio- and a bald crow -Jacob- who are both pets of evil masters, the Sorcerer Beelzebub and the witch Tyrannia Vampirella. <br /><br />This is a fun book with enough of the real world in it to also make it significant in helping children see their surroundings with wiser eyes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4839916267767914007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3622412833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3622412833" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3622412833?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783522185202" href="/book/show/50315805-der-satanarch-ol-genialkoh-llische-wunschpunsch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=german">german</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3622412833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15501447127254960079"><em>Published in English as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27719.The_Night_of_Wishes' title='The Night of Wishes by Michael Ende' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Night of Wishes</a>.</em><br/><br/>Beelzebub Irrwitzer is cornered in his laboratory by one of Hell's emissaries, for not reaching his yearly quota of bad deeds. The dark sorcerer needs to make it up by midnight, or his soul would be collected, regardless of the numerous dastardly deeds that he <em>did</em> in fact complete. After much panicking and hand-wringing, his only choice remains to team up with his aunt, the money witch Tyrannia Vamperl, and hope for the best. Or worst, depending on you</span>
  <span id="freeText15501447127254960079" style="display:none"><em>Published in English as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27719.The_Night_of_Wishes" title="The Night of Wishes by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night of Wishes</a>.</em><br><br>Beelzebub Irrwitzer is cornered in his laboratory by one of Hell's emissaries, for not reaching his yearly quota of bad deeds. The dark sorcerer needs to make it up by midnight, or his soul would be collected, regardless of the numerous dastardly deeds that he <em>did</em> in fact complete. After much panicking and hand-wringing, his only choice remains to team up with his aunt, the money witch Tyrannia Vamperl, and hope for the best. Or worst, depending on your point of view.<br><br>As for the rest of the world? It seems pretty much doomed, unless the evildoers' two familiars manage to set aside their quarrel, long enough to come up with a counter plan.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605549313i/30386521._SX540_.jpg" alt="pets spying" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was pleasantly surprised by this little, 238-page, fairy-tale, especially since my initial interest lay solely in its lengthy (and unpronounceable) title. The naming humor was just brilliant, such as the emissary from Hell being named <em>Maledictus Maggot</em>, and Beelzebub repeatedly calling him <em>Mr. Larvae</em>.<br><br>The mentions of Beelzebub's ecologically harmful chemical experiments, Tyrannia's questionable money-making schemes, and of course the narrator's overall distain of humanity stepping up to save the planet from an impending ecological disaster, the story felt quite contemporary. In other words educational <em>and</em> cute enough for any young reader.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605549313i/30386522._SX540_.jpg" alt="The cast of the story" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As an adult, I was mainly interested in Beelzebub and Tyrannia's adventures. Their attempt at saving the day was much more interesting to follow. Unlike the <em>goodies</em> who heroically brave the elements on the off-chance of finding some help, the <em>baddies</em> actually have a sound plan. Sure, the many (not so) subtle attempts to outwit one another is all but telegraphing inevitable failure. That said, for all the narrator's effort in describing Beelzebub and Tyrannia as the worst possible plague to befall the world, I still found myself rooting for the <em>baddies</em> to escape from Hell's clutches.<br><br><strong>Score: 3.8/5 stars</strong><br><br>My inner child positively <em>adored</em> everything about this story. Lots of magic, talking animals, some action scenes describing some extremely dangerous stunts, unexpected supernatural help, plenty of comedic relief, all nicely wrapped up in a classic-happy-ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15501447127254960079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438736871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9563725697257804920">I have had this book on my to read shelf for a long time. I originally picked it up because itâ€™s by the author of the Neverending Story (which I adore). It ended up being an okay read, but was slow at parts and a bit awkward to read. I think younger readers will enjoy this story more.<br/><br/>The evil sorcerer Beezlebub Preposteror and his equally evil aunt are both behind on their required annual quota of evil deeds. Things start looking better for them when they find a recipe for a potion that can gran</span>
  <span id="freeText9563725697257804920" style="display:none">I have had this book on my to read shelf for a long time. I originally picked it up because itâ€™s by the author of the Neverending Story (which I adore). It ended up being an okay read, but was slow at parts and a bit awkward to read. I think younger readers will enjoy this story more.<br /><br />The evil sorcerer Beezlebub Preposteror and his equally evil aunt are both behind on their required annual quota of evil deeds. Things start looking better for them when they find a recipe for a potion that can grant wishes in reverse. This would be great because not only can they complete their evil deeds they can also fool the animal spies that live with them. Except they donâ€™t know that the cat and raven that live with them have a sneaky plan of their own to stop them.<br /><br />There are some wonderful illustrations throughout this book and I enjoyed those. I found the story to be a bit silly and over the top; itâ€™s something I think younger readers will enjoy more than adults. I personally wasnâ€™t a huge fan though...it was okay but not great.<br /><br />There is a lot in here about friendship and good triumphing over evil. There is also a lot of clever wordplay and some cute poems throughout.<br /><br />The whole story is very predictable and the characters very stereotypical. Itâ€™s a story I think younger readers will enjoy but adults will find a bit boring to get through. I honestly struggled a bit just because I had trouble engaging with the characters and story.<br /><br />Overall an okay read about good triumphing over evil. The animal characters are cute and funny, if a bit over the top. There is some clever word play in here as well. I struggled a bit with the pacing (some parts were kind of boring) and with the way the writing flowed (it was a bit awkward at times). I would definitely recommend The Neverending Story over this book.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5846569732798408309">I got this book for Christmas as a kid and I loved it, so the emotional factor makes it four stars instead of three. What can I say? It's no <i>Neverending Story</i>. It's no <i>Momo</i>. But it's a heartwarming story nonetheless. Two villains are lagging behind their evil quotas, and it's not a good thing to default when hell is your creditor. It's up to a cat and a crow to thwart their schemes on New Years' Eve. A great book to put under a kid's tree for Christmas and hook them into reading.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1545868770931420001">A cat and a raven - animals usually passed to the witch's imagination. And he's right next to some wizards. This time not to help them, but to help an Animal Council, threatened by the destructive world spells of wizards.<br/>Michael Ende writes well. He knows how to compose a story, how to give life to some characters. The cat goes, for example, to the typology of the Italian braggart who, if he does not sing a little, even if false, or does not boast of noble origins, does not feel himself. Also, t</span>
  <span id="freeText1545868770931420001" style="display:none">A cat and a raven - animals usually passed to the witch's imagination. And he's right next to some wizards. This time not to help them, but to help an Animal Council, threatened by the destructive world spells of wizards.<br />Michael Ende writes well. He knows how to compose a story, how to give life to some characters. The cat goes, for example, to the typology of the Italian braggart who, if he does not sing a little, even if false, or does not boast of noble origins, does not feel himself. Also, the sorcerer can only be evil, practicing evil spells, destroyer of the world, pacting with Satan to whom he has some debts. All typology.<br />Can I tell you more about the raven and the evil aunt (a saint also appears at one point) or about Satan's servant? Typologies, although well rendered by Ende.<br />I would have expected, in the good tradition of German writers, that the author would rely more on the grotesque, comic, the inclination towards the diabolical (yes, I liked the Devil's Elixirs). But both the cat and the raven renounced their witchcraft and wanted to be good and thwart the plans of the wicked. He succeeded. But at what price? I lost interest.<br /><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://zupia.ro/index.php/2020/11/11/michael-ende-punci-cu-porunci/">http://zupia.ro/index.php/2020/11/11/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1545868770931420001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_24852832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24852832" />
    <a title="Alice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1247026-alice"><img alt="Alice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285199742p2/1247026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24852832?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice" href="/user/show/1247026-alice">Alice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1247026-alice?shelf=ya-mg-kids">ya-mg-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24852832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13955552565632557247">This is a middle-grade book by the author of <i>The Neverending Story</i>. It's meant to be read in real time, meaning the events take place over the course of five hours, and it's meant to be read in five hours. I suppose if a parent read this to a child, the timeline would line up nicely.<br/><br/>Much of the premise of the book is younger than middle grade: a talking cat and raven, a witch and wizard who are evil because they're evil, and transparent main characters. Jacob, the raven, is clever and observant,</span>
  <span id="freeText13955552565632557247" style="display:none">This is a middle-grade book by the author of <i>The Neverending Story</i>. It's meant to be read in real time, meaning the events take place over the course of five hours, and it's meant to be read in five hours. I suppose if a parent read this to a child, the timeline would line up nicely.<br /><br />Much of the premise of the book is younger than middle grade: a talking cat and raven, a witch and wizard who are evil because they're evil, and transparent main characters. Jacob, the raven, is clever and observant, but cowardly, while Mauriccio, the cat, is easily fooled but brave and loyal. In the end, they're rewarded for their fight to end the evil plot cooked up by their masters, Beelzebub Preposteror and Tyrannia Vampirella, Preposteror's aunt and financier.<br /><br />There are some plays on words within the text, though they may have been harmed from their translation from German. Or, the fact that I'm not the target audience might've made them fall flat.<br /><br />I think a 7- or 8-year old might find this perfectly entertaining as a bedtime story. Adult readers looking for the magic of <i>The Neverending Story</i> would do well to look elsewhere. This is far more simplistic and silly. It does have a few genre convention nods, but, overall, it doesn't stack up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13955552565632557247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106579008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3601832320694595198">While I did enjoy the playful tone and writing style of The Night of Wishes, I wasn't overly impressed by it. The story is simple and straightforward, which wouldn't be a problem if the plot wasn't so incredibly flat, don't expect any twists or much action. In fact, some opportunities for interesting action were quickly bypassed with a single description of "with cunning and great effort," reading that a character is cunning isn't very interesting, I'd like to make that assessment myself by the </span>
  <span id="freeText3601832320694595198" style="display:none">While I did enjoy the playful tone and writing style of The Night of Wishes, I wasn't overly impressed by it. The story is simple and straightforward, which wouldn't be a problem if the plot wasn't so incredibly flat, don't expect any twists or much action. In fact, some opportunities for interesting action were quickly bypassed with a single description of "with cunning and great effort," reading that a character is cunning isn't very interesting, I'd like to make that assessment myself by the character's actions. I'm not sure if there is an overall message in this book, which bothers me. I typically expect a book to have a little something more than just a funny story. I think it was going somewhere with a theme of unlikely friendships, but nothing ever really happened to bind the two friends together beyond the basic plodding along of the plot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3601832320694595198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6970247-razvan-moldovan?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6970247-razvan-moldovan?shelf=1st-quarter">1st-quarter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2965791286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10285490925123095484">On the New Year's Eve, Beelzebub Erezinus receives a visit from an unexpected guest, Mr. Ascaride. He is an emmisary of His Infernal Majesty and came to announce Erezinus that he didn't fulfill his yearly contractual conditions of devastating the world through disease, flood, death and other evil things and, because of this, everything will be taken away from him. Scared because he has only one day left to do this, he joins forces with his aunt, Tyrannja Vamperl, in finding the right solution. O</span>
  <span id="freeText10285490925123095484" style="display:none">On the New Year's Eve, Beelzebub Erezinus receives a visit from an unexpected guest, Mr. Ascaride. He is an emmisary of His Infernal Majesty and came to announce Erezinus that he didn't fulfill his yearly contractual conditions of devastating the world through disease, flood, death and other evil things and, because of this, everything will be taken away from him. Scared because he has only one day left to do this, he joins forces with his aunt, Tyrannja Vamperl, in finding the right solution. On the other side, the forces of good are represented by two animals, the crow Jakob Krakel and the tom cat Maurizio di Mauro. A story of good vs evil, of unusual and unexpected friendship in a time where everything seems lost for the world.<br /><br />When I was a kid I was a big fan of the animated TV Series titled Wunschpunsch. A couple of years ago I found out that the animated series is actually based on this book so I had to get my hands on it and read it. The story was simple, straightforward and easy to follow so it's a cute little book when you want to relax, to read something that doesn't take much energy and concentration. I enjoyed it and I might even check out some episodes of the animated show. I also liked the writing style of Michael Ende and I will definetly read some more of his work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10285490925123095484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9joprqyaIG4Gvaz7jpSUUHUzTwNz3r7NnbaEr08SjRlrretP9BJGSvRL8XyQaBWnxxghx4mLpr3MBds6MQ1bzg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2230290763636873162">Michael Andreas Helmuth Ende was a German writer of fantasy and children's literature. He was the son of the surrealist painter Edgar Ende.<br/><br/>Ende was one of the most popular and famous German authors of the 20th century, mostly due to the enormous success of his children's books. However, Ende was not strictly a childrenâ€™s author, as he also wrote books for adults. Ende claimed, "It is for this chil</span>
  <span id="freeText2230290763636873162" style="display:none">Michael Andreas Helmuth Ende was a German writer of fantasy and children's literature. He was the son of the surrealist painter Edgar Ende.<br /><br />Ende was one of the most popular and famous German authors of the 20th century, mostly due to the enormous success of his children's books. However, Ende was not strictly a childrenâ€™s author, as he also wrote books for adults. Ende claimed, "It is for this child in me, and in all of us, that I tell my stories," and that "[my books are] for any child between 80 and 8 years" (qtd. Senick 95, 97). Endeâ€™s writing could be described as a surreal mixture of reality and fantasy. The reader is often invited to take a more interactive role in the story, and the worlds in his books often mirror our reality, using fantasy to bring light to the problems of an increasingly technological modern society.<br /><br />Ende was also known as a proponent of economic reform, and claimed to have had the concept of aging money in mind when writing <i>Momo</i>. He was interested in and influenced by anthroposophy.<br /><br /><i>Die unendliche Geschichte (The Neverending Story)</i> is Ende's best known work. Other books include <i>Momo</i> and <i>Jim Knopf und Lukas der LokomotivfÃ¼hrer (Jim Button and Luke the Engine Driver)</i>. Michael Ende's works have been translated into more than 40 languages and sold more than 20 million copies, and have been adapted into motion pictures, stage plays, operas and audio books.<br /><br />He died in Stuttgart of stomach cancer.<br /><br />AKA:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16296064.___________" title="ÎœÎ¯Ï‡Î±ÎµÎ» ÎˆÎ½Ï„Îµ" rel="nofollow noopener">ÎœÎ¯Ï‡Î±ÎµÎ» ÎˆÎ½Ï„Îµ</a> (Greek)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2230290763636873162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

With tears in his eyes the little cat tried to straighten out his tail, which no longer looked elegant in the least but had been bent into a zigzag, while the melancholy raven eyed the feathers scattered on the floor, feathers he couldn't really spare. But as is often the case after such bickering, both felt relatively peaceful and ready for reconciliation. Jacob thought he should not have been so rude to the small, fat tomcat, and Maurizio wondered if he might have done something wrong with the poor, unfortunate raven. "Forgive me, please," he mewed. "I'm sorry, too," rasped Jacob.&rdquo;</span>

It is constantly striving for power over Good, but without Good it could not exist â€“ and if it ever achieved total power, it would have to destroy precisely that over which it desires to wield said power. Thatâ€™s why it can last only as long as it is incomplete [â€¦]. If it were complete, it would cancel itself out. Thatâ€™s why it has no place in eternity. Only Good is eternal, for it contains itself without contradiction.&rdquo;</span>
